# The Solar System Reference File

The Solar System is the gravitationally bound system of the Sun and everything that orbits it.
It formed about 4.6 billion years ago from the collapse of a giant molecular cloud.

## The Sun
- Type: G-type main-sequence star (G2V)
- Contains more than 99% of the mass of the Solar System
- Diameter: about 1.39 million km
- Surface temperature: about 5,500°C
- Core temperature: about 15 million°C
- Energy source: nuclear fusion of hydrogen into helium

## Mercury
- Closest planet to the Sun
- Orbital period: 88 Earth days
- No substantial atmosphere
- Extreme temperature swings

## Venus
- Similar in size to Earth
- Thick carbon dioxide atmosphere
- Hottest planetary surface in the Solar System
- Rotates very slowly and in a retrograde direction

## Earth
- Only known world with life
- 71% of the surface is covered by water
- One natural satellite: the Moon
- Atmosphere rich in nitrogen and oxygen

## The Moon
- Average distance from Earth: about 384,400 km
- Causes tides through gravitational interaction
- Likely formed from a giant impact early in Earth's history

## Mars
- Known as the Red Planet
- Home to Olympus Mons, the largest volcano in the Solar System
- Home to Valles Marineris, a vast canyon system
- Two moons: Phobos and Deimos

## Asteroid Belt
- Located between Mars and Jupiter
- Contains millions of rocky bodies
- Largest object: Ceres (a dwarf planet)

## Jupiter
- Largest planet in the Solar System
- Gas giant
- Great Red Spot is a giant storm
- Dozens of moons including Io, Europa, Ganymede, and Callisto

## Saturn
- Famous for its ring system
- Gas giant
- Moon Titan has a thick atmosphere
- Lower density than water

## Uranus
- Ice giant
- Rotates on its side
- Blue-green color due to methane

## Neptune
- Farthest major planet from the Sun
- Strong winds and storms
- Moon Triton likely captured from the Kuiper Belt

## Kuiper Belt
- Region beyond Neptune
- Contains many icy objects
- Home to Pluto and other dwarf planets

## Pluto
- Classified as a dwarf planet
- Discovered in 1930
- Large moon: Charon

## Oort Cloud
- Hypothetical spherical reservoir of comets
- Extends far beyond the Kuiper Belt
